URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS28602747	2021-01-03 12:46:15.024736	10553	species	Red-breasted Sapsucker	Sphyrapicus ruber			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Washoe	US-NV-031	US-NV_2211	15			Tahoe Meadows	L125288	H	39.3038595	-119.9141857	2004-08-21	08:15:00	obsr16674	S1729885	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	240	4.828		1	1		0	1	0		I hiked the Ophir Trail again this morning (August 21), at the west end of Mt. Rose Meadows, Washoe County.  I saw some interesting birds, but perhaps more interesting were the birds I *didn't* see.  No Western Wood-Pewees, no Fox Sparrows, no Hermit Warblers, only a scattering of Yellow-rumps, and no Brewer's Blackbirds.  Meanwhile, Nutcrackers were very active today, and I saw a few of them every time I looked into the sky.	I also saw a weird-looking sapsucker. It had a rather longish gray bill, a red forecrown contrasting with gray hindcrown and back of neck, white malar,and a red throat that didn't appear to continue on to the breast at all.  Other attributes: white shoulder patch, barred primaries, barred tail, variable white barring up the mantle, grayish flanks with a slight yellow wash on the belly, and it lacked contrasting black-and-white on the face and breast.  Overall it was drab, confusingly plain, and unimpressive. Photos.
